Wusong Health District to be Established 79

There used to be a model health district in Wusong Town, which was jointly operated by the Medical School of National Central University and the Municipal Health Bureau. After the January 28th Incident, it was unfortunately suspended. Last year, President Weng Zhilong of Tongji University and Professor Li Xuanguo of the university negotiated with Li Tingan, the Director of the Health Bureau, to resume it and requested assistance from the Health Department. An agreement has been reached and it is said that it can be realized soon. A committee will be set up to take charge of this health district, and the expenses will be shared by the Health Bureau and Tongji University. The Shanghai Lottery Association has allocated 30,000 yuan as temporary expenses for the opening. Once it is restored in the future, the public health of the Wusong area will definitely improve, the health of citizens will be protected, and the students of the Public Health Department of the Medical School of Tongji University will have more places for practice, which is truly a win-win situation.

Representatives of the National Postal Workers' General Union Return to Shanghai from Petition in Beijing 80

The Petition Did Not Have Results

The National Postal Workers' General Union of this city convened an emergency meeting a few days ago to discuss the postal unrest in Tianjin and Beiping. Everyone agreed that the peaceful policy has completely failed. In addition to issuing a notice to the postal workers' unions in various places to actively prepare for vigorous preparations, it also sent four representatives, including Zhang Kechang, to Beijing to petition the central government and the Ministry of Communications, hoping to obtain a satisfactory solution. The petition representatives have returned to Shanghai yesterday. According to them, the Ministry of Communications did not give a satisfactory answer to the requests and did not accept the suspension of dispatching the members in Tianjin and Beiping and the cancellation of the demotion punishment. Even the punishment of Ba Lidi and Cao Jianting was not approved. Currently, the emotions of postal workers in various places are agitated and the postal unrest is about to expand.

Strike at the Welfare Rubber Factory Resolved 81

Detained Workers Released on Bail by the Municipal Party Department

The entire workforce of the Great China Welfare Rubber Factory in Xingjiazhai, Zhabei, recently organized a labor union and investigated worker names, causing a misunderstanding by the factory. Fourteen workers were detained, leading to a strike. The detained workers have now been released on bail by the Municipal Party Department, and the workers have all resumed work. The following is a record of the events:

The Incident The entire workforce of the factory, in order to organize the Rubber Workers' Union of the Fourth District, had submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department for permission and dispatched Fan Guoren of the Civil Affairs Section as an instructor. In order to clarify the content of the workers, Fan recently sent a letter to the worker Wu Fushou, asking him to investigate the names of all the workers. After receiving the letter, Wu collected all the workers' workbooks to copy the names. The matter was discovered by the factory, which misunderstood that Wu Fushou had other purposes, and then stopped him. Wu then adopted a tough attitude, resulting in a conflict. The police were then called and detained by the First Precinct of the Fifth District. Some unemployed workers, such as Zhu Caixing, gathered workers in a secret meeting in Yuanmaoli, Tiantong Road, that evening. The instructor of the Municipal Party Department found out and reported that the workers were illegally gathering, and then reported it to the Third Precinct of the Fifth District, which dispatched police to detain the workers Zhu Caixing, Qin ChanGen, Li RongYang, Ji Sheng, and other ten people, and sent them to the Zhabei Judicial Section for disposal.

Workers Released on Bail After the workers were detained, the entire workforce declared a strike the next morning and sent representatives to the Municipal Party Department to petition. The day before yesterday, the Municipal Party Department sent Fan Guoren to persuade the workers, instructing them not to be exploited by reactionary elements, and advised them to resume work first. As for the arrested workers, the Municipal Party Department would be responsible for bail. The workers then stated that their actions were indeed wrong, they were willing to repent, and accepted the advice. The Municipal Party Department then notified the Zhabei Judicial Section by telephone to release all the detained workers on bail. All the male and female workers in the factory have resumed work yesterday morning, declaring a solution.

Sun Hegao and Others Preparing to Establish a Copper Rolling Mill 82

Former Directors of the Two Railway Bureaus, Sun Hegao, and former Headquarters Chief of Staff Yu Zhongnan, and others believe that various industries are controlled by foreigners, and the required machinery parts are supplied by Japanese merchants, so the rights and interests are lost and the leakage is increasing day by day. Therefore, they are raising huge amounts of money to establish a large-scale copper rolling mill and are hiring Yu Dingming, the former Director of the Taixian Construction Bureau, as an engineer. Since the factory was initiated and prepared, it has been progressing very smoothly and will be officially opened next month. Its name is the China Copper Rolling Mill, and the factory address is on Qu Zhenren Road, Xiejiao, Shanghai, with the office located at No. 4, Niansi Road, Weihaiwei Road, British Concession. It is reported that the main machinery of the factory is custom-made from Germany, so the delivery of goods in the future will definitely be fast and excellent.

Consulate in Lyon Investigates Shanghai Silk Merchants 83

Preparing to Develop Chinese Silk Trade in Europe

And Inviting Participation in International Exhibitions

Mr. Zou Zhihua of the Chinese Consulate Office in Lyon, France, yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to investigate the names and addresses of Shanghai silk merchants. The original letter stated, Respectfully, After Zihua was ordered by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to set up an office in Lyon in November last year, it has been actively prepared and has been completed and started working. Lyon is the commercial center of France for the Far East, especially for velvet products. Its international trade relationship with our country is extremely important. Since the establishment of this office, it is planned to first focus on Lyon and prepare for the development of China's silk weaving industry in Europe. However, during the investigation, more actual materials from our country are needed for comparison. Therefore, I specifically ask the President of your esteemed association to lead the group, solicit solid silk merchants in Shanghai who are interested in international trade, and contribute their opinions. There are several items that are requested to be indicated in detail here, listed as follows: (1) Store name and address; (2) Product name in Chinese and English; (3) Samples for exporters must be classified, priced and sent to Lyon; (4) Method of delivery and payment; (5) Other. In March of this year, Lyon routinely holds an international commodity exhibition. If Shanghai's business community intends to participate, then the above items are requested to be actively carried out. Furthermore, please send as much as possible the journals published by the committee on commercial affairs and store them for future reference in case foreign merchants inquire, etc. It is reported that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has approved the Business Affairs Section to send personnel to the Silk Factory Industry, Electrical Silk Weaving Industry, and Silk Satin Industry, and other public associations for investigation.

County Construction Bureau Abolished 84

County Government Establishes Technical and Health Office

The question of abolishing the Shanghai County Construction Bureau arose because the county government moved to Beiqiao, where construction was heavy. It was once said that the bureau would not be abolished for the time being. Now it is understood that the county government has received a provincial order to abolish the bureau and merge it into the county government. The county will set up a technical office to plan construction matters. It is said that the current director of the bureau, Sun Shengzeng, will still serve as the director of the technical office, and Shi Jingyuan and others will be technicians. The deadline for the merger is March 1st, so Director Sun is currently handling the handover procedures.

Patriotic Enthusiasm of Songjiang Elementary School Students 85

Running Away From Home to Join the Army in Shanghai

Jiang Bingqiu, the son of Jiang Maolong, who lives at Malu Bridge outside the West Gate of Songjiang, is fourteen years old and is a student at the local elementary school. Recently, he heard his teacher in school talk about the invasion of the eastern provinces by the violent Japanese, and now they have invaded Rehe again. The situation is becoming increasingly serious. Although Bingqiu is an underage boy, he is extremely indignant. He has twice gone to the local military police camp to request to be enlisted and sent north to fight the enemy. The battalion commander, seeing his youth and bravery, praised him greatly and kindly advised him to serve the country after he has completed his studies. It would not be too late. He then ordered someone to send him home. Unexpectedly, on the afternoon of the 19th of this month, Jiang, together with Meng Guiren (nicknamed Little Girl), the fifteen-year-old son of Meng Tubiao, a carpenter living next door (and a classmate of Jiang), took a fourth-class train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line to Shanghai. Before leaving, they only took two silver dollars. After deducting the fare for the two, they still had a few dimes. However, they had no relatives in Shanghai, and they were lost and confused. They searched everywhere for places to enlist, but after running around for two days, they found nothing. They had no choice but to beg along the way. Later, Lu Xisheng, a native of Songjiang who runs the Yunjian Inn in Yuqing Lane, Xixin Bridge Street, in the French Concession, took them in out of consideration for their fellow hometown relationship. He asked them why they came to Shanghai, and the two students told him the truth. After learning about it, Lu sent a letter to the two students' families, asking them to come to Shanghai to take them back home. After receiving the letter, Jiang and Meng came to Shanghai yesterday to take their children home for a reunion.

Records of the Christian Ten-Person Group and Educational Leaders Meeting 86

Telegraphing to Christian in Nation Unite Arouse

Initiate National Salvation Savings to Prepare for Relief

The Chinese Christian National Salvation Ten-Person Group held a meeting of Shanghai district church leaders at 3:00 PM yesterday on the fifth floor of the Shanghai YMCA in the French Concession. Those present included Li Denghui, Fan Dingjiu, Wei Shaozeng, Wu Shan, Zhou Zhiyu, Huang Meixian, Xie Songsan, Pang Zixian, Shao Changgeng, Ye Zaiqing, Yao Xianyang, Jin Xianqing, Wang Timothy, Yu Zhizhai, Zhou Meicun, Li Hengchun, and over sixty others. Zhao Jinqing presided, Weng Guoxun recorded, and Zhu Guishen prayed. The chairman reported that the country's situation is critical, social morality is deteriorating, and human desires are rampant, the harm of which is immeasurable. The reason for this is that Christians do not emphasize faith and action. Mr. Zhang Zhijiang and others, in view of this, initiated the organization of the Ten-Person Group, hoping to save people and the country. It is expected that all the comrades present will understand this. Now, please ask Mr. Zhang to report on the preparations. Mr. Zhang stood up and said that the purpose of the group's initiation is that we Christians should uphold the spirit of Jesus' love, sacrifice, and fearlessness, promote truth, and jointly face national difficulties, awaken compatriots across the country, and together repent and confess sins before God, reform ourselves, save ourselves and the country, love and help each other, regardless of denomination, cooperate and actively carry out our mission. Preparations and progress in both Beijing and Shanghai have been quite smooth. However, this matter is of great importance and requires the joint responsibility of all comrades present in order to glorify God and save the country from danger. He also suggested that those who have not yet been listed as initiators should all be initiators, which was unanimously approved. It was also decided that the preparatory committee would consist of fifteen people. In addition to the original seven, eight additional people were elected, including Ding Shujing, Lin Hongbing, You Shuxun, Wang Wanbai, Xie Songyang, Shen Weixin, and Zhu Haoran. The election of You Hui was approved. Next, the proposals were discussed: 1. Telegraphing to Christians in countries around the world to pray for our national difficulties, uphold justice, and eliminate the scourge of war. 2. Telegraphing to Chinese Christians at home and abroad to pray for the country, unite and rise up, and jointly seek salvation. 3. Initiate national salvation savings to prepare for relief work. All three proposals were unanimously approved, and it was decided that starting today, for one week, at noon each day, to pray for the country. All churches and believers should participate. Dr. Cheng Jingyi then offered a prayer of blessing, and the meeting adjourned with refreshments. The second preparatory meeting is scheduled for 6:00 PM today at the same location to discuss and decide on the implementation of the proposals.

Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia Telegraph Request to Postpone Postal Rate Increase 87

The Postal Administration submitted a proposal to the Ministry of Communications on the 7th of this month to increase postal rates for letters to Southeast Asia. The Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce believes that this move will affect the livelihoods of overseas Chinese and has telegraphed its opposition. The following is an excerpt from the telegram: To Chairman Chen of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee in Nanjing: According to a letter from the Min-Chao Remittance Association, business conditions are extremely bad, and remittances from overseas Chinese have sharply decreased. Family members at home are already suffering. Now, the postal rate for letters is about to increase to one dime and two and a half cents, which is like adding weight to a fish. The more remittances decrease, the more difficult it becomes for families to make a living. We earnestly request that your committee be concerned about the difficulties of overseas Chinese and ask the Ministry of Communications to postpone the increase so that the people can be relieved and have something to rely on for support. Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce respectfully.

Mr. Wu Zhihui's Discussion on the "New Popular Medicine Series" 90

Mr. Ding Zhongyu from Wuxi, after claiming to have completed the annotation of "Jie Xue Gu Lin," immediately began compiling the "New Popular Medicine Series" with the hope of instilling new medical knowledge into the people of the whole country, thereby strengthening the people and the nation, which would have a great impact. This book is currently being printed and will soon be published. Mr. Wu Zhihui has written a preface to the book, which is very valuable. The excerpt is as follows:

Stubborn me is relatively healthy, so I have lived to sixty-nine years old this year without any major illnesses. I agree with what is said in the "Book of Han" that "if a disease is not treated, it is often cured by traditional Chinese medicine." I have never consulted a doctor for minor colds and fevers. I also believe that some medicines, passed down from my grandmother and others, such as hawthorn ash for diarrhea, fritillaria cirrhosa steamed with snow pear for coughs, etc., work. As suggested by new trends, such as quinine pills for malaria, or swallowing a few Santonin tablets, they often work, so I do not despise Astragalus and Ginseng, serums, or radium tablets. Whether it's traditional Chinese medicine or Western medicine, I only think about the five organs corresponding to the five elements, and removing all my teeth can be a preparation for curing diseases, but I don't have faith in them to that extent. However, to be frank, luckily, Heaven has taken care of me. I have never suffered from typhoid fever or pneumonia, nor have I had carbuncles or boils, so I have not had the opportunity to test the skills of doctors. However, for the prevention of such dangerous diseases, such as fresh air and clean diet, I also believe in making choices when necessary, although I seem to not care. When my appetite is not right for fatty and delicious fish and shellfish or for devouring large portions of fish and meat, I also know to stop eating, although I seem to not be picky about good or bad food. I can try to practice relatively reasonable common sense hygiene, but I haven't researched it in detail. However, I also vomited blood when I was young. I saw in medical books that "if you vomit blood and don't die, you will definitely be scared to death." I closed the book, and I had a sudden realization. Therefore, I immediately acted as if I was already dead, and immediately regulated my diet and sleep, leisurely and content. In the afternoon, I took a walk in the suburbs, looking up at the white snow, stretching across the horizon, opening my mind and chest. Sitting quietly and listening to the sparrows chirping in front of the eaves, it was as beautiful as a sheng and a reed pipe. Haha, in less than twenty days, I nourished myself so that I had a fat head and big ears, and I stopped vomiting blood, and it never happened again. What I find most funny is the so-called "getting rid of the root." Anyone who hopes to get rid of the root of a disease gets flustered and hurriedly calls for a doctor, blaming heaven and cursing the earth, entrusting their life to the doctor (and entrusting their life to the Bodhisattva is even more ridiculous). I don't really agree with this. I sometimes laugh at them for courting death. Therefore, although I don't believe in medicine, and I live a casual life, I unexpectedly use my patience and care to deal with minor illnesses. For example, for tooth medicine, I deliberately ask what is called pain, and consider the degree of pain, seeing how far it goes. I only feel a warm, helpless sensation. Sometimes I can't lift my arm, and I think, why rush to cure it? Let it rest, saving some movement. I believe that using natural therapies may also be helpful. However, in the end, it is still my barbarity. Fortunately, I rely on my relatively strong body, which cannot be considered as valuable experience for others to refer to. However, I have been friends with Mr. Ding Zhongyu for fifty years. We are often shocked by his weak body. We don't say it out loud, but we worry in our hearts that he is definitely not going to live long. In addition, his efforts in learning and handling affairs are extraordinary. Even his earnestness in studying medicine and treating diseases means that he has used medicine to cure many people with weak bodies, which doesn't further deplete his spirit? How is it that he doesn't seem to be doing anything? I think he must be using medicine to treat himself, so he has actually reached the age of sixty, and his body has become stronger. However, I hear that he doesn't easily take medicine, but keeps his mind calm and peaceful, rarely gets angry, and rarely gets impatient. That's why I understand that he really understands natural therapy. I often call his method of maintaining health the "sage's method," and I recommend it to everyone who doesn't understand natural therapy and relies solely on medicine, telling them to learn from it. Now he has selected and introduced various natural therapies such as air, sunlight, diet, and exercise. Only then did I realize that he originally possessed this skill. Although he has a deep understanding of these things, and I only have a superficial understanding, I firmly believe that I am a healthy old man who relies on nature, and he is a healthy and long-lived man who creates his own health. After reading his book, I am even more convinced that I am on the right path. His lamp has guided me, and I can walk more skillfully. Therefore, on the occasion of the publication of the twenty volumes of the "New Popular Medicine Series," I dare to add some nonsense at the beginning of the book, even though I don't understand medicine at all, so that people who are as stubborn as me, and people who are as weak as Mr. Ding, can all refer to it. However, although I firmly believe that diseases need the help of natural therapies, if I contract epidemic diseases or infectious diseases, I also believe that it is absolutely necessary to use medicine for prevention or to consult a doctor, and that one cannot rely solely on natural therapies in such situations. Fortunately, Mr. Ding's book also contains more detailed and concise methods of drug prevention, or advice on how to treat them, for us. This is truly an essential book that everyone should keep with them. Mr. Ding has obtained the secret to longevity and hopes that everyone will live to be eight hundred years old. We should also thank him. Okay, I've said too much nonsense. I'll send it to Mr. Ding for a laugh. February, 22nd year of the Republic of China, Wu Jingheng.

Minutes of the 131st Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Lawyers Association 91

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened the 131st joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committee members at its clubhouse at the intersection of Rue Bellesort and Avenue Foch in the French Concession at 7 p.m. the night before. Committee members Shen Junru, Zhu Fojiu, Shi Liang, Yan Yinwu, Liu Shifang, Chen Tingrui, Jiang Jiemin, Lu Dingkui, Shi Ying, Zhou Shiying, Yang Zhihao, and others publicly elected Lu Dingkui as chairman, and Dai Xisheng as secretary. The meeting began as follows: The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, and then the proposals were discussed. (1) Committee member Shen Junru reported on his participation in the Shanghai All-Circles Comfort the Soldiers at the Frontlines Committee and proposed that the association purchase additional comfort items. (Resolution) It was resolved to use the remaining donation of $4,151.16 from the previous Economic Committee to purchase pot helmets or telescopes, etc., and send them to the frontlines. (2) Committee member Li Shirui was rumored to be secretly ordered to be arrested and should submit a statement to the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government for clarification. (Resolution) Passed, the telegram will be drafted and sent immediately. (3) Members Ge Zhaoji and others proposed to donate money to purchase airplanes and anti-aircraft guns. (4) The National Lawyers Association sent a letter urging donations for airplanes. (Resolution) The above two cases were handed over to three committee members, Zhu Fojiu, Chen Tingrui, and Shen Junru, for review. (5) The former Anti-Japanese Association's Sales Committee requested to temporarily borrow the association's third-floor rooms as a clubhouse. (Resolution) Approved to use two rooms on the third floor for a period of three months. If the committee is unable to conclude its work and relocate by the deadline, it must first obtain the association's consent. Committee members Shen Junru and Shi Ying were appointed as representatives to attend. (6) Should the date of the association's spring general meeting be determined? (Resolution) It was decided to convene the spring general meeting at 2 p.m. on March 26, and the location was tentatively borrowed from the Lake Society. It was also decided to convene a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committee members on February 8. (7) The Shanghai District Court replied regarding the proposal for joint litigation, stating that if there is no situation as described in Article 424 of the Code of Civil Procedure, it will be enforced in accordance with the law. (8) The Shanghai First Special District Court replied regarding the joint litigation, stating that in order to execute a portion of the judgment first, it is necessary to request a certificate of unfinalized appeal from the appellate court in accordance with Article 190 of the Code of Civil Procedure. (Resolution) The above two cases were combined and sent to all members for review. (9) The Shanghai First Special District Court Prosecutor's Office replied that the China Legal Guidance Society case was closed on February 1 of this year. (Resolution) Filed. (10) Member Lu Shaozong sent a letter resigning from his position as a replacement executive committee member. (Resolution) Please invite member Lu Shaozong to take office on a specific date. (11) Lawyer Cha Nanchang replied that he was unable to comply with the payment of the construction fund. (Resolution) Reply to the lawyer requesting that he still follow the association's previous letter. (12) Member Zhang Deqin replied that there was no real estate department, only a rental office that collected rent on behalf of others, and requested that it be filed. (Resolution) Filed. (13) The Shanghai Accountants Association replied recommending accountants Qin Kai and Xie Lin to handle the association's financial accounts for the second half of the 21st year and requested that future matters be handled directly by member accountants. (Resolution) Filed. (14) Member Yang Changchi inquired whether it is legal for a lawyer to establish a branch office in a county government district. (Resolution) Reply to the member that the act does not comply with legal regulations. (15) Member Qian Ying inquired whether a lawyer should appear in court with the qualification of a lawyer when handling matters stipulated in Article 21 of the association's rules. (Resolution) Reply to the member that since he is acting as a legal representative, he can appear in court with the qualification of a lawyer. (16) Lawyers Guo Shouyi, Chen Guangyu, Li Yilin, Cheng Qian, Shi Baoliang, Zhang Huansheng, Wu Zhaozhen, Ding Xuan, Dong Zhongjiang, Xue Yangsu, and others applied for membership. (Resolution) Approved, and reported to the courts at all levels on the same day. The meeting adjourned late at night.

A Bomb Found in the General Headquarters of the Flower Association 93

There is a flower association general headquarters with the longest qualifications, located in Sanxin Lane, Dujiazhai, Route Wagner, French Concession. It is said that the flower association was opened by a gambler named Mao. The night before, a bomb was suddenly discovered in the headquarters. Fortunately, it was discovered early and did not explode. Measures were immediately taken to remove it. However, the police have already learned about it and are currently conducting a thorough investigation.

A Bizarre Case of an Old Man and a Young Girl 94

Suspected of Being Sold to Fujian

Yesterday morning around 11:00 a.m., police officers Jiang Zhengde and others from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team were patrolling the river near the Dada Wharf and saw the Wanxiang steamship berthed there, not yet set to sail. They immediately boarded the ship to conduct an inspection. They found an old man in the cabin carrying a young girl, looking flustered and suspicious. When questioned, the two were evasive. They were immediately taken to the team. During the preliminary interrogation by Chief Zhu, the old man stated that his name was Yang Huachen, 55 years old, from Zhejiang. The girl was his niece, and he intended to take her to Fujian to find a relative. When the girl was questioned, she said that her name was Zhu Alin, 16 years old, and the old man was her maternal grandfather. This time, he was taking her to Fujian to find her aunt. Since the statements of the two were completely different, and since there was no reason to take a girl thousands of miles away to find relatives, it was clear that there was a case of trafficking involved. They were ordered to prepare a document and send it to the bureau for investigation.

Swindlers Using Checks as a Tool 95

Zhang Jiawei and Others Fled

Swindlers Zhang Jiawei, Zheng Hanshan, Xu Xiuzhang, Shen Yunlai, and Wu Wanlong rented a house at 595 Xinzha Road in October of last year, established the Baohua Store, deposited a small amount of money in the World Commerce & Savings Bank, and obtained the bank's checkbook. They then purchased goods from various manufacturers, paying the price with checks. After operating for more than a month, they swindled several thousand dollars worth of goods. When the checks were due, these people, fearing that the scam would be exposed, fled in advance. When the various factories went to the bank to cash the checks, they were unable to do so. When they went to the Shinhua Store to claim payment, the store was already closed, with a sign posted saying "rent due for business failure." Only then did they realize that they had been swindled. At present, the factories that have been swindled, such as Youcheng Silk Factory, Asia Silk Weaving Factory, Zhenhua Umbrella Factory, Huanan Knitting Factory, Yishenghao, Tianhehao, Longchanghao, etc., have hired lawyers to file a criminal self-accusation against the swindlers in the First Special District Court, requesting that they be arrested and investigated and ordered to repay the goods, totaling more than 1,000 yuan. However, the swindlers have already flown away, and it is unknown whether they will be caught in the future.

The Shih Shih Hsin Pao Agrees to Provide Compensation to Wang Wei San 96

Reply to the Journalists Association

The Shanghai Journalists Association, for the case of Wang Weisan, a reporter stationed in Beijing for the Shih Shih Hsin Pao, who was kidnapped and shot by thugs, and who was in dire straits after his death, resolved at an executive committee meeting to send a telegram to the garrison headquarters police department to arrest the murderers, and to send a letter to the Shih Shih Hsin Pao to provide compensation. The association received the newspaper's reply yesterday, stating: "In response to your letter, we have learned that Mr. Wang Weisan, our reporter stationed in Beijing, died unjustly. We are grateful for your concern and high regard. When the incident occurred, our newspaper immediately arranged for the Beijing office to handle all funeral arrangements. Furthermore, Mr. Wang Yingjie, the director of the enemy consulate, personally went to Beijing a few days ago to inform the garrison headquarters to arrest the murderers and bring them to justice in order to comfort his spirit. As for Mr. Wang's family, they have already been compensated in accordance with the company's regulations. Thank you again for your attention. We hereby reply."

The China Jockey Club's Gold Cup Race to be Changed to a Charity Champagne Raffle 97

To be held on April 30th in 引翔

許静仁, Chairman of the Shanghai Temporary Relief Association for the Henan, Anhui, and Hubei Disaster Areas, along with 張嘯林 and 杜月笙, Directors of the Shanghai China Jockey Club, decided to hold a charity champagne raffle. A special meeting was convened yesterday at 4:00 PM at the逸圍 Greyhound Racing Track, inviting leaders from all sectors to discuss ticket sales. The response was extremely enthusiastic, with 39,400 tickets, more than one-third of the total, being sold on the spot. The details are as follows:

Attendees

Approximately one hundred individuals were present, including 吳鐵城, 戴戟, 熊秉三, 黄涵之, 趙晉卿, 穆藕初, 王曉籟, 虞洽卿, 袁履登, 鄔志豪, 黄伯度, 郭德華, 張竹平, 王彬彥, 劉鴻生, 章行嚴, 應時, 沈錫慶, 文鴻恩, 王一亭, 江一平等.

Chairman's Report

Chairman 许静仁 opened the meeting with a report on its purpose, stating that it was to organize a charity champagne raffle to raise funds for the disaster areas of Henan and Anhui. He welcomed all those present, noting that they all shared a commitment to charity and relief, and would not hesitate to help those in need. He thanked 张啸林 and 杜月笙 for donating this year's Gold Cup Race to the association. He then gave a brief report on the disaster situation in the three provinces, stating that on October 6th of the previous year, the Relief Committee forwarded a telegram from Commander-in-Chief Chiang, stating that the recovered areas of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei had been devastated for a long time, with widespread suffering, vast numbers of refugees, and widespread devastation. All trees were felled, all houses burned, and even chickens and dogs were not spared. Millions of refugees were left destitute and starving, and the disaster was severe. He requested that funds be raised for relief and that various sectors organize inspection teams to visit the disaster areas for on-site inspections. After deliberation, it was decided to unite all sectors and launch this association, which was established on October 11th at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Fundraising and relief efforts were launched alongside a disaster area inspection, in the hope of doing their best to fulfill their duties. The most severely affected counties in the three provinces, and the areas visited by the association's inspection teams, were reported to those present and are presented below: (A) Severely affected counties in the recovered areas of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei provinces: (1) Henan Province: seven counties: 经扶, 立煌, 商城, 潢川, 光山, 罗山, 信阳; (2) Anhui Province: five counties: 六安, 霍邱, 英山, 霍山, 寿县; (3) Hubei Province: thirteen counties: 黄安, 罗田, 阳新, 沔阳, 潜江, 监利, 汉川, 天门, 应城, 京山, 通山, 厂城, 通城. (B) Organization of the association's inspection teams and locations of their inspections (omitted); (C) Overview of the disaster situation in various counties: (1) 罗田: In areas such as the 阳河 district and the 凤凰山 district, nine out of ten homes were empty, and refugees lacked food and clothing, resulting in a tragic situation; (2) 英山: The county had been a bandit area for a long time and suffered greatly. Most of the houses in the urban area were destroyed, and seven or eight out of ten people fled. People ate grass roots and tree bark to survive, and corpses were piled up everywhere. The Hongshan priest initiated the construction of two white bone towers to bury them; (3) 六安: The disaster situation was particularly severe from the county seat to the 蔴埠 area, with at least one thousand people dead in the least affected areas, and about three to five thousand in the most affected areas. 蔴埠 was in the bandit zone, where over ten thousand people died. The people are now struggling for food, and grain prices have soared. Disaster victims have no clothes to keep warm, and countless people are starving to death; (4) 光山; (5) 经扶; (6) 罗山; (7) 信阳: In the above four counties, houses and farming tools were almost completely destroyed, and hundreds of thousands of people fled. Corpses were everywhere, presenting a terrible sight. It is said that there are two places for burning people, 烧人塲 and 红厂, within 经扶 county, both used for killings, with over 20,000 people killed. 罗山 is suffering from an extreme shortage of grain and clothing, and the sale of sons and daughters is common; (8) 汉川: The county seat was not breached, but the rural areas suffered greatly. The local organization is still good, and there is a Communist Suppression Volunteer Army of 8,100 people; (9) 天门: The areas near 岳口镇 were mostly devastated. The 別家大灣 area was completely burned, a truly tragic sight; (10) 潜江: The area is close to Honghu Lake and is a gateway for the Communists. It has been captured and lost over 20 times, with over 70,000 deaths. Shops have no capital of over 300 yuan, and people still wear single layers of clothing and eat tree bark, making it extremely miserable; (11) 监利: There is not a single copper coin that can be exchanged in the city, the doors are wide open, and many people have fled; (12) 潢川: The county and 焦澤湖 have been lost and regained many times and have suffered particularly severely. Only the elderly and children were seen along the way, with no adult men. Furthermore, there has been no rain for several months, making the situation extremely dire; (13) Other counties: The severity of the disaster situation will be announced later, as the reports have not yet been fully compiled; (D) The urgency of disaster victims awaiting relief: Due to the impact of the current situation, the association has received very little in donations, while the number of disaster victims in the three provinces is huge and in urgent need of relief. Furthermore, groups in the disaster areas of Jiangxi and Shaanxi provinces have requested to join the association and help raise funds. The suffering of the disaster victims is extreme, and the association's resources are stretched thin. If a way is not found to quickly raise large sums of money, it is feared that the surviving people will be beyond help. As the saying goes, "Not saving is certain death, and delayed saving is also death." This would not only fail the expectations of the disaster victims in the three provinces but also go against the initial intentions of the public to do good and provide disaster relief. He respectfully requested that everyone join together to perform this act of kindness, avert this catastrophe, and save the remaining people. He also gave a supplementary report on the overview of the Northeast relief efforts.

Other Reports

(A) Mayor 吴铁城 spoke on the current situation in the disaster areas of the three provinces; (B) 熊秉三 reported on the tragic situation of refugees from the Northeast fleeing to Tianjin and Beijing; (C) 张啸林 reported that relief for refugees could not be delayed and urged all those present to provide as much assistance as possible; (D) 王晓籁 reported on the Gold Cup Race event, stating that there would be a total of 110,000 tickets, with 10,000 tickets being given away as gifts. For every book purchased (10 tickets), one ticket would be given away. Each ticket would be sold for ten yuan, for a total of one million yuan. The first prize would be 420,000 yuan (70%), the second prize would be 120,000 yuan (20%), the third prize would be 60,000 yuan (10%), and small prizes would be 150,000 yuan (20%). The drawing would be held on April 30th in 引翔. These tickets are now on sale. The main sales office is the China Jockey Club on 静安寺 Road, and branch sales offices are at the 申報, 新聞報, 先施, 永安, 新新, and 麗華 companies, for a total of 15 locations.

Number of Tickets Pledged

王彬彦 and others personally carried donation books and asked everyone to sign and pledge the number of tickets they would sell. A total of 39,400 tickets were sold on the spot, accounting for more than one-third of the total. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Proposed Advertisement

A draft advertisement was also prepared on the spot, which will be sent to various newspapers for publication today. The original text stated: "Due to the repeated disasters in the three provinces, the devastation is unbearable to describe. Although the gentlemen and merchants of this port have raised funds for relief, the area is vast and the disaster is severe, making it difficult to provide comprehensive assistance. Therefore, this association, at the request of the Shanghai Temporary Relief Association for the Henan, Anhui, and Hubei Disaster Areas, has decided to donate this year's Gold Cup Race to the association so that the income can be used for relief funds, in order to fulfill our limited responsibility. The main points of the arrangements are outlined below for your information. There are 110,000 Gold Cup Champagne Raffle tickets, with 10,000 tickets being given away as gifts. For every book purchased (10 tickets), one ticket will be given away. Each ticket will be sold for ten yuan, for a total of one million yuan. After deducting 250,000 yuan for commissions, all proceeds will be used to expand the relief funds. The remaining amount will be distributed as follows: 420,000 yuan (70%) for the first prize, 120,000 yuan (20%) for the second prize, 60,000 yuan (10%) for the third prize, and 150,000 yuan (20%) for small prizes. The above amounts are based on the premise of selling out all the tickets. The drawing will be held on April 30th at the racecourse of this association in 引翔. Tickets are now on sale. Please purchase them from this association at No. 770 静安寺 Road, or send a postal money order. You will be saving disaster victims, increasing wealth, and seizing a good opportunity. Signed, 张啸林 and 杜月笙, Directors of the Shanghai China Jockey Club."

Further News on the Tragic Shooting of Chinese by Vietnamese Police 98

The Court Inspects the Bodies of Zhu Guting and Liu Fugao

The Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association Requests Punishment of the Culprit and Compensation

On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 1:45 PM, Vietnamese Constable No. 427 of the麦兰 police station in the French Concession, while investigating two women riding together in a rickshaw, tried to inspect their passes. A dispute arose with the rickshaw puller, 沈芳荣, and the passengers, 解莲贞 and 张凤英. In the ensuing altercation, a Cantonese man, 朱固廷, who was walking by, was shot and killed on the spot. 刘福高, 赵长兴, and 徐林生 were also wounded in the abdomen and arms. The responsible police station took the Vietnamese constable, the rickshaw puller, and Ms. 徐 into custody for investigation. The injured 刘 and 赵 were sent to仁濟 and 廣慈 hospitals for treatment. 徐 went to seek medical attention herself. Zhu's body was taken to the 同仁輔元 sub-hall for examination. 刘 also died. The details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It has been learned that 刘福高 died at 11:53 PM last night. The hospital notified the police station to take the body to the coroner's office. Yesterday, the Second Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor 邓葆蓀, along with forensic doctor姜 and clerk 卢世臣, arrived at noon for the inspection. The French police station also sent a Western detective and a doctor from the 工部局 to the scene. The bodies were inspected according to the law, and the case was heard. Zhu's family, 朱固海, reported that his brother, 朱固廷, had been tragically shot and killed and requested justice. As no relatives of Liu were present, the official ordered the inspection to confirm that 朱固廷 and 刘 had died from gunshot wounds. 朱's body was allowed to be claimed by his brother for burial. Liu's body was photographed and buried by the 同仁輔元堂, awaiting family claim. It is reported that the families of the deceased have reported the information to their fellow-villagers associations and requested assistance.

Furthermore, the Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai was very concerned after learning of the death of their fellow villager, 刘福高. In addition to sending personnel to the Chaozhou Native Association in Shanghai to inquire about the handling of the death of the Cantonese man, 朱国廷, they also sent a letter to the Police Department of the French Municipal Council and the Second District Court of the Special Zone, urging them to punish the culprit and provide compensation according to law. The letter stated, "Respectfully, according to my fellow villager, 刘庆来, his nephew, 刘福高, a native of Cixi, 39 years old, was working as a warehouseman in the Yuan Tai Heng sugar store on 洋行街. On the afternoon of the 25th of this month, he was passing by 新桥街 in the French Concession when an Annamite constable inexplicably opened fire and shot 福高 in the abdomen. He immediately fell to the ground, unconscious, and was taken to the 仁濟 Hospital, where he died around 12 o'clock that night. Qinglai was shocked and went to see him, but it was too late. However, his nephew, 福高, came from a poor family, with an elderly mother over sixty years old and a wife and children below, crying for food. This unexpected disaster has left them without a way to live. Therefore, we earnestly request assistance to comfort the wronged soul." It is our belief that the Vietnamese constable opened fire in a busy street during the day, killing and injuring many people, which is a blatant disregard for human life. Based on the above, we urgently request your director (court) to punish him according to law and provide appropriate compensation to comfort the bereaved family."

Russian Woman Dies

Autopsy Required to Investigate Abortion Issue 99

Husband Unaware of Wife's Abortion

Neighboring Woman Testifies to Deceased's Statement

A Russian woman named 阿納司旦雪印諾開締納恊可寗 (translated name), 29 years old, whose husband, 恊可寗, is an employee of the Shanghai Power Company, residing at No. 47 Tangshan Road, became pregnant four months ago. On January 7th of this year, due to her aversion to childbirth, she went to a Russian midwife in 茂海 Road to have an abortion. The midwife performed the procedure at that time. Since then, the woman experienced heavy bleeding in her lower body and difficulty walking. Her husband noticed that his wife's condition was worsening and sent her to 宏恩 and 公濟 hospitals for treatment, but to no avail. She died at around 10 AM on the day before yesterday. The hospital reported the case to the 汇山 police station, which sent detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the斐伦 Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court was notified, and Prosecutor 郭炜 arrived to inspect the body and hear the case. A Russian woman named 司各立, residing at No. 31 Tangshan Road, testified that she had visited the deceased's home a few days ago and was told that she had had an abortion in early January and had been bleeding ever since, and had not left the house since then. The deceased's husband, 協可寗, testified that the deceased was his wife. She did not explain this to me at first. Later, I went to the hospital and questioned her repeatedly, and she finally admitted to having had an abortion and said that she had no money to bury her. Based on the testimonies, Mr. Guo stated that it was not yet certain that the deceased had died from the abortion and that an autopsy was required to determine the truth. He ordered that an autopsy be performed and that the hearing be postponed to next Tuesday. The body was handed over to the Health Department of the 工部局 for preservation.

Great Unity of Chinese River Steamers 100

Resisting the Monopoly of Foreign Shipping Companies

Last year, when the Sichuan war broke out, large quantities of piece goods and cotton yarn ordered in Chongqing and 泸州 and other ports were suspended from shipment and accumulated in Shanghai. As the river water receded, the goods were still not shipped. Recently, the Sichuanese merchants, due to the end of the war and the gradual increase in water upstream, and fearing that the Yangtze River transportation might be disrupted, wired Shanghai to rush the goods. This has led to a trend of foreign shipping companies competing to monopolize transportation and Chinese shipping companies uniting to resist. A summary of the situation is reported below:

Foreign Ships Compete for Navigation 101

Due to the Sichuan war last year, a large amount of cargo was blocked in Shanghai, mostly foreign cloth and cotton yarn. Recently, the Sichuanese merchants repeatedly wired Shanghai to ship the goods to prevent disruption of the Yangtze River transportation. These yarns and cloths are transported by two routes: one is direct Shanghai to Chongqing ships, and the other is Shanghai to Yichang ships, which are then transferred to Chongqing. The foreign merchants specializing in the Sichuan River shipping route in Shanghai are the Jardine River Company, which has a total of twelve ships operating, followed by 太古怡和, which also has more than ten ships. Currently, Jardine is competing to carry the direct Chongqing cargo, and 太古怡和 is dividing the Yichang transfer cargo. The competition is now underway.

Water Freight Increases 102

The main cargo for Sichuan River transportation is cotton yarn. In previous years, foreign shipping companies drastically reduced freight rates to as low as six taels of silver per piece in the shortest time to defeat the Chinese shipping companies, causing many small Sichuan River shipping companies to suspend operations. Seeing the success of the price reduction strategy, the foreign merchants gradually increased freight rates again in the autumn and winter of last year. The cotton yarn water freight rate rose from six taels to eight taels, then from eight taels to ten taels, and then from ten taels to twelve taels, more than doubling it. Special water freight rates are required during shallow water periods.

Chinese Ships Unite 103

Last year, seven or eight small Sichuan River shipping companies were squeezed out by foreign ships and went bankrupt. At that time, the Chinese merchant Minsheng Company raised capital and bought up all the suspended ships, with the idea of consolidating the fragmented forces and preventing the Sichuan River navigation rights from falling completely into the hands of foreigners. The Minsheng Shipping Company suddenly rose and also launched Shanghai-Chongqing, Shanghai-Yichang, Hankou-Yichang, and 泸州 routes with more than ten ships, such as the Minquan and Minzhu, to compete with Jardine and other foreign merchants. This time, the Sichuanese merchants rushed to load the accumulated cargo, and the foreign ships took the opportunity to increase freight rates. Minsheng Company joined forces with 招商, 三北, 永兴, 浹江渝 and other Chinese shipping companies to form the Great Alliance of Chinese River Steamers to gather strength and regain navigation rights.

The company will break the foreign ships' monopoly and has decided to reduce freight rates for all goods shipped from Shanghai to various parts of Sichuan from March 1st. It has also notified the Sichuanese merchants in Shanghai. Yesterday, the foreign shipping companies in the port received an urgent telegram from Yichang reporting that the Great Unity of Chinese Ships has been established and is completely aimed at resisting foreign merchants. They should jointly discuss ways to salvage the situation. The foreign merchants who received the news are also secretly discussing countermeasures.

王正廷 left for Hangzhou on the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train at 9:30 AM yesterday.

曾仲鸣 and 高凌百 returned to the capital by night train last night.

Young Woman Attempts Suicide in Lake, Rescued 105

At 7:35 PM last night, a young woman suddenly jumped into the lake at the Nine-Bend Bridge in the lake-center pavilion of the City God Temple in the Nanshi district. Fortunately, a nearby police officer spotted her and managed to rescue her. However, she had been in the water for quite some time and had swallowed too much water, rendering her unconscious. The woman was wearing a dark blue patterned wool cheongsam and cotton trousers. Her shoes were missing. Her hairstyle was a half-modern style, indicating that she was a semi-modern young woman. She was immediately taken to the Second Precinct of the First District. After questioning her in detail, the precinct chief found that the woman did not utter a word. She was first sent to the Shanghai Hospital. She regained consciousness this morning and, after further questioning, revealed some of the facts. She claimed that she was 26 years old and married a man surnamed Bao at the age of 22. Bao died shortly after due to illness. She then cohabited with a man surnamed Zhao, who was a merchant selling opium. Zhao had an 18-year-old younger brother who was fond of wandering. This spring, he even joined a gang of bandits and committed robbery in the French Concession. Zhao's brother was arrested. Unexpectedly, he intended to falsely accuse her (the young woman claimed). Her home was searched by the police station and was left empty, and her cohabiting partner also disappeared. Because she had become homeless, she had the idea of suicide. Director Liu, according to the report, immediately prepared a document to submit it for further judicial interrogation.

Fire Alarm on Avenue Joffre Last Night

At 10:09 PM last night, a fire suddenly broke out on the upper floor of the Zhou Xiexiang tobacco and paper shop at No. 90 Avenue Joffre, at the intersection of Avenue Foch in the French Concession. Due to the old nature of the surrounding buildings, which were easily combustible, the fire quickly spread to No. 88, a cross-street building in Taiping Lane to the left, No. 86, the facade of the Qingzhen religious hall, and the entire building of No. 92, the 道生印尉所, and No. 94, the 正大橡皮店, to the right. After the fire department drove to the scene and made strenuous efforts to extinguish the fire, it was not extinguished until 11:35 PM. A total of four buildings were destroyed.

Robbery Case on Haichang Road 106

At 6:10 PM last night, six robbers suddenly broke into the home of Sheng Yin at 建右呈 on Haichang Road in the jurisdiction of the Fourth District of Zhabei. They brandished pistols, warning them not to make any noise. They wantonly searched the house, upstairs and downstairs, for about half an hour before fleeing with their loot. After the incident, an examination revealed that gold jewelry, furs, and approximately 400 yuan in cash were stolen. The owner filed a report with the Fourth District Headquarters requesting investigation and arrest.

Bigamy or Treating Both Wives Equally 110

Officials Urge Husband to Treat Both Wives Equally

Ordering Xie Yuchun to Support Liu Lanying

Liu Lanying, a young woman from Wuxi, recently hired lawyer Xu Lin to apply for mediation with the local court mediation office regarding her husband, Xie Yuchun (i.e., Xu Yuchun), who abandoned her and is demanding payment of 3,000 yuan in alimony. Briefly, because the defendant sent someone to marry Ms. Wang as his wife on October 14th of last year. When the petitioner married into the family, the defendant claimed that his previous wife had died and treated the petitioner as an equal wife, treating her as a servant, etc. Yesterday, Wang Shicheng was appointed to open the court for trial. The petitioner, Liu Lanying, testified to the previous situation. When asked, the defendant Xie Yuchun, who is 34 years old, from Wuxi, and lives at No. 17 Xinfeng Lane, Menghua Street, inside the West Gate, replied that he works as a newspaper vendor. Because my original wife was ill and could not have children, through someone's introduction, the petitioner had nowhere to go, so she was brought by Yuan Lai and lived together. Not long after, my wife died of illness. Because the petitioner could not manage the household affairs, I married Ms. Wang to fill the position. The petitioner's bedroom is in the pavilion, and she must sleep until ten o'clock every day before getting up, and often finds fault, placing her clothes elsewhere. Now I have no money, and even if I did, it would be difficult to agree. The official said that she is still a member of the family, and you must treat her equally. The official then attempted to reconcile both parties in court. As a result, in addition to the man being responsible for the petitioner's food, clothing, and housing, she will also receive a monthly allowance of two yuan for pocket money and continue to live together. There must be no abusive behavior. A reconciliation was reached, and both parties signed and left the court.

Reader Advisor 113

Work and Love

丨丨Reply to Mr. Wei Ying丨丨

Answer: I have read your letter and will reply briefly as follows: (1) Apprenticeship problem. You have many contradictions in your view of apprenticeship: First, you say: "I [feel that being an apprentice, except for being] scolded by the master and suffering physical losses, my spirit is extremely happy." This is probably a kind of politeness and not a heartfelt statement, because you "[think that] doing work [is] not a long-term plan." Isn't this a contradiction? Second, if a person is beaten and scolded, their spirit is still extremely happy. I am afraid that this is not the case. What exactly are you happy about? Isn't this a contradiction? Third, if you say you are willing to be an apprentice, but you hope to be promoted to an employee every day, isn't this a contradiction? Fourth, you say: "[Muddy gray face, oil-stained clothes...a typical example of Chinese life]," in fact, this cannot be regarded as a typical example of Chinese life. Workers in developed countries around the world are all like this. Can you rely on your muddy gray face and oil-stained clothes alone to "[keep pace with the great powers]?" This statement is also unclear. If it is said that China's future depends on the muddy gray faces and oil-stained clothes of these people taking on the burden, this is correct, but the purpose of this burden is not to "[keep pace with the great powers]." On the contrary, it is to overthrow the social factors that cause this keeping pace, because keeping pace means competing for leadership, means fighting for hegemony, and means the evil manifestation of imperialism's plunder and exploitation of colonies. Since you are willing to be a worker, but you are still dreaming the imperialist dream, isn't this a contradiction? (2) Marriage problem. You are in love with the daughter of your former store owner, so problems will naturally arise: First, you are an apprentice, and he is the store owner; second, he has money, and you are a poor boy. This is not only an ordinary problem of status, but a very serious problem of wealth and poverty. The urgent problem to be solved in front of you is this: do you climb to his position to reach up to him? Or does he give up and sweep away everything to descend to your position, willing to share the hardships with you? If he comes to condescend to you, that is something we should praise. If you abandon the apprentice society and the worker society in which you live in order to pursue your lover, then you are also limited. In our opinion, the only thing that can be done today is this: (1) You wholeheartedly do your apprenticeship, and then become an independent worker. You must seek common welfare for the masses of your "[muddy gray face, oil-stained clothes]" society. If you "[look at that mountain and think] that mountain is higher," and you want to be promoted to an employee or become a boss all day long, then you are wrong. (2) Write a frank and open letter to your boss's daughter, clearly telling him that you are now an apprentice and that your future life will only be the life of a worker. If she is willing to always love you, then she can only give up her status as the store owner's daughter to live with you, a gray-faced brother. Otherwise, break up with him and go your own way in life. In the society of muddy gray faces and oil-stained clothes, you can find a lover with a muddy gray face and oil-stained clothes. Such lovers have equal status, the same interests, and can naturally enjoy the joy of harmonious love. If you do not give up, and you must "[a toad wants to eat swan meat]," then you are just asking for trouble. Even if you desperately fly into the sky and eat swan meat, you will fall down and break your legs and bones, and ruin your life! Honest words are offensive to the ear. I know that my humble opinion cannot be accepted by you, but other than this, we have no other good plan to offer. I hope you will think twice.

Donations to Universities in Beiping and Tianjin 114

丨20% to be used for anti-Japanese expenses

(Beiping, 26th) Regarding the issue of anti-Japanese donations from universities in Beiping and Tianjin, the Salvation Federation has passed a resolution to donate 20% of the academy's operating expenses for anti-Japanese expenses and has sent representatives to negotiate with various colleges and universities, which is gradually making progress. Xu Songming said that there are no problems with anti-Japanese donations from various colleges and universities. Jiang Menglin said that the professors at Peking University have not yet reached a consensus on anti-Japanese donations and will decide after he has smoothed things out. The Peking University Academic Affairs Committee decided to donate 5% of their monthly salary from January to March, for a total of three months. If necessary, the amount and time of the donation can be increased. Yang Likui, a standing committee member of the Education Federation, said that he advocates that professors donate one month's salary, because the peasants in the front line are still donating three or four yuan per person and donating rice for large carts for transportation. They are a hundred times more bitter than professors. Central figures who usually eat well and wear good clothes and sit in luxury cars should donate more enthusiastically.

(Qingjiangpu, 26th) At the plenary session of the Huaiyin Normal School staff on the afternoon of the 26th, a proposal was made to suggest that the provincial education federation donate salaries to purchase airplanes to resist Japan and save the country. The result was extraordinarily satisfactory.

Handover by the Huaiyin Education Bureau 116

Since the Huaiyin Education Bureau was ordered to close, it has been handling the handover procedures in preparation for sending it to the Third Section of the County Government for acceptance. Both parties have submitted a request to the county government for approval.

Tsinghua University is on the Verge of Shaking its Foundations 117

If American Indemnity Payments are Stopped Again, the School Will Inevitably Shut Down

Students Will Hold a General Meeting to Support the Principal

The China Education and Culture Foundation Will Also do Everything Possible to Maintain it

(Beiping Correspondence) The funding for National Tsinghua University has always been sufficient. When the national universities in Beiping and Tianjin were in financial straits, only Tsinghua University, which was far away from the city of Beiping, still had magnificent and luxurious school buildings, and various buildings were being added as much as possible, because the school's funding was entirely allocated from the American Boxer Indemnity refunds, and was not affected by the Russian Boxer Indemnity like other national universities. However, last year, the Japanese robbed the Northeast customs duties, and the Ministry of Finance announced that it would suspend the American and British Boxer Indemnity payments for one year starting in March. This was the first time that Tsinghua University's funding was affected by the situation. Later, after the school principal Mei Yiqi went to Beijing several times to negotiate, the Ministry of Finance finally approved a loan of one million yuan to the school during the suspension period to provide some assistance. Recently, acting Premier Song Ziwen, due to the impending national crisis, urgently needs funds, and plans to suspend the American, British, and Italian Boxer Indemnity payments for another year. He also has concerns about the impact of American Indemnity payments on education and cultural groups. This is the second time that Tsinghua University's funding has been affected by the situation. The following is a record of the situation of the school and the China Education and Culture Foundation regarding the current funding problem.

Remarks by President Mei of Tsinghua University 118

Tsinghua University relies entirely on the American Boxer Indemnity refund for its funding. Now, the American Boxer Indemnity refund is about to be suspended for another year, and Tsinghua's foundation is likely to be shaken. On the 22nd, a reporter made a special trip to Tsinghua Garden to interview President Mei Yi-qi and inquire about the financial situation. The following is a record of Mei's remarks: Reports stating that the school's funding is still sustainable are inaccurate. Since the suspension of the Boxer Indemnity refund in March of last year, the school has felt the pain of the funding source being cut off. Subsequently, with the government's permission, 125,000 yuan was allocated monthly from July of last year to February of this year for subsidies. However, the school's annual operating expenses require 1.2 million yuan, and the expenses for students studying in the United States require over 700,000 yuan annually. Furthermore, with the addition of the School of Engineering and a sharp increase in the number of faculty and students, there is an urgent need to add a great deal of equipment. A subsidy of one million yuan is truly insufficient. However, given the critical situation during the Shanghai war last year, we had no choice but to endure it for the time being. On the one hand, we appropriately halted several construction projects and used part of the construction funds to subsidize school expenses. On the other hand, we tried our best to economize, postponing anything that could be delayed. Over the past year, the school has been struggling financially. In the past two months, the situation has become even more difficult. We have tried to negotiate extensions for many payments due, hoping to pay them after the funding increases in March. Maintaining daily expenses has already necessitated borrowing from banks. Recently, I read in the newspaper that the Boxer Indemnity refund is about to be suspended again. If this is true, then the school will inevitably be brought to a standstill, because the situation this year is very different from last year. Therefore, the faculty and students of the school are extremely uneasy. A few days ago, I accompanied Mr. Ren Hongjun, the secretary-general of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, to Peiping to request an audience with Minister Song, but we were unable to meet him due to unforeseen circumstances. We still do not know the true situation or whether it has been confirmed. However, I believe that during this time of national crisis, the government's finances are certainly difficult. While the amount of the American Boxer Indemnity refund is relatively small in the government's revenue and expenditure, it is crucial for the maintenance of this school and the China Foundation. In the coming year, in addition to the school's regular expenses of 1.2 million yuan and the American expenses of over 700,000 yuan, the equipment for the two new departments of electrical and mechanical engineering, which the school is adding in accordance with the government's directive to develop science and engineering, will cost at least 2 million yuan, which is still far from enough. If the suspension is actually implemented, and only the remaining funds that should be used as a foundation are taken by the government, it may not provide much assistance to the government, but it will have a great impact on the school's repeated exhortations to students to study diligently and strive to serve the country. Moreover, if the precedent of suspending payments is opened again and again, and if it continues, the foundation of the school will be shaken, and it will be difficult to maintain it in the future, let alone develop it and achieve success. Furthermore, yesterday's newspaper reported Minister Song's remarks that, in any case, the educational expenses of Peiping and Tianjin would not be affected, which shows that the government attaches importance to education and considers it a major national plan, which is in line with our views. Although the school has not yet made many contributions in academics, judging by its equipment and achievements, it is still one of the better universities in the country. The government should not be biased and allow it to come to a standstill. Even if the Boxer Indemnity refund is not suspended, the funds for March will not be received until April, so there will be no way to manage next month. We will have to find a way to borrow. In short, the proposal to suspend the American Boxer Indemnity refund again will not provide much assistance to the country, but it will greatly harm the school. I hope that it will not become a reality, so that the studies of more than 900 young people in the school can be spared from suspension, the 80 or 90 students studying in the United States will not be stranded overseas, university education will not be affected, and the foundation of the country will not be shaken, which would be a great fortune.

Opinions of Tsinghua Student Representatives 119

The reporter interviewed Shang Chuandao, the representative of the Tsinghua University Student Union, and asked about the students' attitude towards the funding problem. His answer was as follows: Unfortunately, our school suffered the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund for one year last year. Thanks to President Mei's trip to the capital for negotiations and the students' efforts as a backing, the Ministry of Finance allocated a loan of one million yuan during the suspension period. Unexpectedly, the American Boxer Indemnity refund is about to be suspended again this year, which is an unfortunate situation for our school. In the spring of last year, Tsinghua, in order to add the School of Engineering and departments such as electrical and mechanical engineering, requested the government to approve the allocation of all the American Boxer Indemnity refunds due to our school in the final year of the fiscal year (i.e., from January to June of the 21st year of the Republic) as school expenses, which was approved by the government. Subsequently, due to the Japanese seizure of Northeast tariffs, the Ministry of Finance suddenly announced the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund for one year from March, causing Tsinghua University, which was in the process of expansion, to suddenly feel an economic panic. Although the Ministry of Finance allocated a loan of one million yuan afterwards, it was far from the school's original funding, which was two million yuan. Only after adopting reduction measures could we barely survive the difficult situation. The last time the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture held a regular meeting in Shanghai, this issue was discussed, and Director Ren Hongjun contacted the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance, but without results. Now, President Song has announced the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund for another year, and our school's future is in great danger. The students are considering this difficult problem. For the sake of the studies of all students, we must not allow the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund again. If Tsinghua's funding has problems again, then the addition of courses and departments will be greatly hindered. Not only will the students at Tsinghua be sacrificed in their studies, but the graduate students studying overseas will have no way to make a living. Tsinghua's funding has always been allocated monthly by the customs from the American Boxer Indemnity refund to the American Embassy as a procedure for returning the Boxer Indemnity, and then the American Embassy handed it over to the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, and then the Foundation divided the funds into three parts, one part for the use of students studying in the United States, one part for Tsinghua's regular expenses, and another part for Tsinghua's foundation. Although our school has a foundation, no one can use it. Last year, during the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund, it was stipulated that the American Boxer Indemnity refund would be delayed for one year. The American Boxer Indemnity refund was originally scheduled to be paid off in the 29th year of the Republic, but it was postponed for one year to the end of the 30th year of the Republic. Now there is news of another one-year suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund. Whether it will continue to be postponed for another year will be known after President Mei contacts the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance. In the future, after the American Boxer Indemnity refund is paid off, Tsinghua's funding will completely depend on the interest of the foundation, so the foundation must never be used and must be preserved properly, because the government has no special [funds] allocated to Tsinghua's funding. At present, the students are temporarily silent, waiting for the government to see if there is a solution for Tsinghua's funding after the continued suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund, and waiting for President Mei to contact the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Finance first. All the students pledge to be a backing, and when necessary, convene a general assembly to discuss detailed measures, the purpose of which is to prevent Tsinghua University from closing its doors.

Cultural Institutions in Peiping Affected 120

The reporter learned that in addition to Tsinghua University, the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture was also greatly affected by the suspension of the American Boxer Indemnity refund. He specially interviewed Yu Shangchen, the secretary of the Foundation, who said the following: I also learned from the newspaper that the American Boxer Indemnity refund would be suspended for another year. The exact news will have to wait until the end of April, because that is when the customs surplus period is. Looking back at the suspension of the Boxer Indemnity refund last year, the subsidies for cultural and educational institutions in Peiping were maintained by the Ministry of Finance borrowing one million to maintain the status quo. This amount also included a small amount of foreign debt, which was barely enough to pay. Therefore, the subsidies for existing cultural institutions were greatly reduced, and new establishments requesting subsidies were not approved. Among them, although there were many well-run institutions that should have been subsidized, we wanted to support them as much as possible, but due to financial constraints, we had to cut them off. The Foundation manages subsidies for cultural institutions in Peiping, amounting to about 3 million yuan. Tsinghua's 2 million yuan is also handled by the Foundation. If the American Boxer Indemnity refund is suspended again this year, not only will the status quo not be maintained, but also the foreign debt borrowed last year and the increase in the foundation will be difficult to find other ways. Institutions such as the Jing Sheng Biological Investigation Institute and the National Peiping Library are medium-sized cultural institutions that receive subsidies from the Foundation. Therefore, last year, due to the lack of funds for purchasing books, valuable books that should have been collected were lost abroad, which is a great pity. As for the Foundation's annual meeting, it is held once a year in July, and the location is decided by the Standing Committee. The Standing Committee discussed the location of this year's annual meeting in January, and due to the current situation, it is planned to be determined according to the situation at that time. This is also a special situation this year.

Ministry of Education's Work Report for January 121

The Ministry of Education recently submitted its work report for January of this year to the Executive Yuan for record. The original report is as follows:

(1) Higher Education

(1) Matters related to universities and specialized schools: Peiping Private North China College was poorly managed and was ordered to comply with previous orders and close down as soon as possible. The Guangdong Provincial Industrial Specialized School was approved to be reorganized into a School of Engineering, named Qin Gong College. (2) Matters related to studying abroad: Four public-funded study abroad certificates were approved and issued, one for studying in the United Kingdom and three for studying in the United States. Thirty-seven self-funded study abroad certificates were approved and issued, three for studying in the United Kingdom, four for studying in Germany, five for studying in France, twenty-four for studying in Japan, and one for studying in Denmark.

(2) Secondary Education

(1) Drafting regulations for normal schools. (2) Completing regulations for middle schools. (3) Drafting regulations for vocational supplementary schools. (4) Approving and filing a list of secondary schools in January: Peiyuan Junior Middle School, Henan; Heling Yinghua Middle School, Fujian; Minfan Girls' Junior Vocational School, Hunan.

(3) Elementary Education

(1) Completing regulations for elementary schools. (2) Drafting an outline of implementation measures for career guidance for elementary and secondary school students. (3) Revising civic training in elementary schools. (4) Approving and filing a list of overseas Chinese elementary schools in January: Yu Xi Overseas Chinese Elementary School, Hawaii; She Lu Chinese Elementary School, Seattle.

(4) Social Education

(1) Consulting the Nanjing Municipal Government on the case of the 160 yuan budget for the Capital Experimental People's Education Center in Nanjing, requesting that it be handled as usual from January of the 22nd year of the Republic and notified. (3) Replying to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' letter inquiring whether to participate in the Milan International Film Competition, the Film Censor Committee has been ordered to transfer the order to various domestic film companies to participate. (4) Jointly consulting the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs with the Ministry of Interior to negotiate the punishment of cinemas in the Shanghai Concession. (5) Instructing the Hunan Provincial Department of Education to review the rules of the School for the Blind and Deaf reported, and there are still places that should be revised. Please order them to revise according to the list and submit them for review again.
