(7) Ordering Zhang Jiong, the department director, to be a member of the Ministry's Sports Committee. (8) Writing to Mr. Niu Tischen, Chen Jianxiu, Gao Jian Si, Lei Binnan, Yu Xitang, Chen Zhengjiang, Meng Xiancheng, Shang Zhongyi, Liang Shuming, Sun Ze Rang, Yan Yangchu, Chen Zuosan, Li Jinghan, Xiang Juju, etc., that the Ministry has scheduled a meeting on February 1 to discuss various matters concerning mass education, hoping that they will attend the meeting on time. (5) Ordering the Antiquities Preservation Committee to follow the order of the Executive Yuan to organize the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee in accordance with the resolution passed by the 82nd meeting of the Executive Yuan and to transfer the order for compliance. (10) Replying to the Executive Yuan that Zhang Jiong and Huang Jianzhong have been selected to be members of the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee. (11) Approving the establishment of the Sun Yat-sen Cultural and Educational Center Preparatory Committee. (12) Ordering the Fujian Provincial Department of Education to report the plan for compulsory literacy education in Fuzhou City after inspection and verification, and there is nothing inappropriate. Please implement it in accordance with the plan. (13) Consulting the Ministry of Industry to send the draft reply to the Shandong Provincial Government regarding the review of the draft implementation rules for labor education in Shandong Province.

(5) Mongolian and Tibetan Education

(1) Consulting the Ministry of Finance and requesting the allocation of funds for Mongolian and Tibetan education in accordance with the order of the Executive Yuan. (2) The first, second and third volumes of the Chinese-Mongolian bilingual national language textbook and the first volume of the short-term elementary school textbook have been printed and bound by the Ministry. One hundred copies per banner were distributed to the joint office of the Mongolian leagues and banners in Beijing for distribution and application by the Inner Mongolian leagues and banners.

Local News

Joint Graduation Ceremony for All Municipal Supplementary Schools 122

Over 500 Attendees Including Party and Government Representatives, Teachers, and Students

Chairman Pan Gongzhan Reports on the Situation of Civilian Supplementary Schools

The eighth session of the Municipal Public Schools and the fifth session of the supplementary schools organized by the Municipal Bureau of Education were held yesterday at 2:00 PM at the Municipal Public Education Center. Those in attendance included Mayor Wu's representative, Zhang Yuanruo, representative of the Municipal Party Department, Huang Shaoxiong, representative of the Municipal Health Bureau, Xu Xingjia, Director of the Bureau of Education, Pan Gongzhan, Section Chief Chen Bai, Commissioner Zhang Yongchun, Director of the Public Education Center, Yang Peiwen, and over 500 teachers and students from public schools and supplementary schools. Chairman Pan, the Director of the Bureau of Education, performed the ceremony as scheduled. First, the chairman reported, saying roughly that the meaning of opening public schools and supplementary schools is probably understood by everyone, because the general public has exceeded the age of education and has not been able to study, and some have not been able to study due to family relations. We run these schools to provide learning opportunities for the general out-of-school public, at least to give them a kind of general knowledge. This session of public schools runs a total of 35 schools, with a total funding of 3,474 yuan, an average of 100 yuan for each school. There are a total of 1,697 students, and 384 graduates have been reported, but the exact number is more than that. The average cost per student is 2 yuan. From the first session to the eighth session, the total funding is 37,273 yuan, the total number of students is 13,578, and the total number of graduates (not including the eighth session) is 7,099. There have been five sessions of supplementary schools, with a total of 5,908 students and a total funding of 23,265 yuan, with an average cost per student of 4 yuan. In the future, we hope that the education funding will increase, and we are more willing to expand these schools. At the same time, we hope that private individuals or organizations will work hard to promote them, so that the number of literate citizens will increase day by day. As for the graduates, they should bear the responsibility of advising and guiding. We sincerely hope that these schools will develop day by day and that the public's reading will increase day by day. Next, Mayor Wu's representative Zhang Yuanruo, representative of the Municipal Party Department Huang Shaoxiong, representative of the Health Bureau Xu Xingjia, and Commissioner of the Municipal Bureau of Education Zhang Yongchun gave consecutive speeches, and the graduates' representative gave a reply speech. Director Pan then distributed souvenirs, and the ceremony ended.

Fundraising for Shanghai School Aircraft No. 1 Begins on March 1st 124

The Municipal Education Association has formulated fundraising measures for Shanghai School Aircraft No. 1 and distributed them to major primary and secondary schools in the city. Fundraising will begin on March 1st, with an estimated amount of 150,000 yuan. Elementary school teachers and students will raise 70,000 yuan, and teachers and students of universities and middle schools will each raise 40,000 yuan. It will be carried out in two phases: the first phase from March to June, and the second phase from August to November. We are sending them to you with this letter. Please check and handle them."

Baoshan Public Education Center Mobile National Crisis Exhibition 125

Moved to Gucun for Exhibition

The mobile national crisis exhibition held by the Baoshan County Public Education Center has been exhibited successively in Shengxiang District and Luodian and other places. Yesterday, the exhibits were transported to Gucun for exhibition. It is said that the content of this exhibition is extremely rich, and the causes and consequences of the Wannian Massacre, the September 18th Incident, and the Songhu Bloody Battle last year, as well as the situation of the Japanese brutally killing our compatriots, are depicted nakedly in the form of paintings. After the public visited, they were all filled with righteous indignation. Yesterday morning, an opening ceremony was held, and more than 2,000 people from schools, public organizations, and the public participated. After the meeting, the director of the Public Education Center, Zhu Xuedian, reported on the significance of the national crisis exhibition and how the public can jointly save the crisis. Subsequently, Gu Jimei, Gu Liren, Shun Hongfei and others gave consecutive speeches, which were impassioned, and all the audience was moved.

Vocational Society and Nanjing Road Business Association Promote Vocational Supplementary Education 127

The China Vocational Education Society and the Nanjing Road Business Association have jointly formed a Vocational Supplementary Education Committee, with representatives from each side. It has been decided to add supplementary schools on Nanjing Road next semester to vigorously promote vocational supplementary education, and Jiang Wenyu and Zhou Juchen have been elected as chairman and vice chairman, respectively, to prepare everything.

The 11th World Games Will Be Held in Rome 135

Germany's Poor Economy, Hitler Opposes Holding Games in Germany

Italian Prime Minister Mussolini Has Agreed to Host

(Rome Correspondence) At last year's 10th World Games held in Los Angeles, USA, the Olympic Committee resolved that the next games would be held in Berlin, Germany, in 1936. The German committee members also accepted this proposal. However, at that time, Hitler, the leader of the German National Socialist Party, declared that if he were to lead the German cabinet, he would oppose the next games being hosted by the Germans because the unstable German national economy could not afford such waste. At that time, the Los Angeles newspapers reported this news one after another, and the sports circles of various countries felt extremely uneasy. Recently, Hitler was indeed appointed Prime Minister of the German Cabinet. A month ago, he made a statement to reporters from the German Nazi Daily, saying that he was determined to oppose the next games being held in Germany. Count Razi Ruber, Chairman of the Olympic Committee, was extremely worried when he heard the news. He believed that Italy and Japan were currently competing to host the 12th Games. Since the 11th Games could not be held in Germany, it would be better to move the next games to Italy and formally decide that the 12th Games would be hosted by Japan. Razi Ruber personally visited Italian Prime Minister Mussolini for this matter, and Mussolini agreed to host the next games. Therefore, it is now rumored in Europe that the next games will be held in Rome instead of Berlin.

Spring and Autumn

Shanghai Small Talk 144

— T. G.

Small talk is intended to be different from the idle chatter of Hu Yan. In fact, small talk is just idle chatter. Because I'm afraid someone will misunderstand me or have the ambition to imply [literary archetype], so it's better to call it "small talk."

According to old Shanghai locals who are familiar with local customs, once you wear a [otter fur coat] with Chinese dress or a [tuxedo] with Western dress, you don't take rickshaws anymore. This is naturally related to status and face.

Therefore, not wearing an otter fur coat and taking a rickshaw is obviously a bit out of place, especially on Nanjing Road. Because rickshaws are not allowed on the tram tracks on that most refined street of Shanghai, and can only go close to the sidewalk.

If we're ranking things, if a rickshaw is considered a third-class vehicle, then the taxi of a bill broker probably only deserves to be labeled as [unclassifiable]. It doesn't dare to imitate cars and trams and gallop on the wide road, nor is it patient enough to slowly walk along with the rickshaws following pedestrians. The shouts and yells constantly give the rickshaw pullers a kind of mental disturbance and threat. Unfortunately, I can't represent the rickshaw pullers, and sometimes I really want to turn around and say: "Are you in a hurry? If you're so capable, go run in the middle of the road!"

To avoid the crowding on the trams, I actually subscribed to a monthly rickshaw in the morning (which of course can't be said to be bourgeois). Whenever the hot white foam from the horse's mouth splashed on my collar, I seemed to smell a fishy and rotten stench and couldn't help but curse. At the same time, it makes me miss the sculling boats of my hometown very much. Although it is very small, it can leisurely row in the middle of the river without being interfered with by the river police. As for the mood of listening to the rustling sound of rain on the awning in the cabin, it's something that Shanghai people who are stuck in a cage-like rickshaw canopy can't even dream of!

The Law of the Jungle 145

— Xianxian

Righting wrongs when seeing injustice and drawing a sword to help—if these two phrases haven't yet become antiques in the [Chinese Cultural Museum] and are only worthy of admiration and praise, then Da Erwen's theory of the law of the jungle isn't worth burning by Qin Shi Huang. It can only be put together with scrap metal and sold as waste by the pound. Don't believe it? Look at the facts.

Hooligans—or "green skins" as they're called in the north—harassing decent women on the street. Readers, unless you've never left your house, you've probably seen it once or twice in this smoky society. So, let's use this as an example.

A nice lady walks alone on the street, and a green skin spots her and follows her, talking nonsense and even groping her. If the lady is timid, she'll just let the green skin harass her, taking two steps at a time, her face red and her head lowered, trying to avoid him. Then, not only will the green skin get his way, but even the well-mannered bystanders will crane their necks and applaud. But if the lady isn't easy to mess with and grabs the green skin by the collar after he lets out a fart and slaps him twice, then someone will immediately come to mediate and perhaps the police will even arrest the green skin and bring him to justice.

Japan has bullied China enough. After taking away the Northeast provinces, China simply didn't resist. It was like a rare and pleasing woman letting the green skin harass her. Who saw anyone righting wrongs and drawing a sword to help? When the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army resisted in Shanghai, just like the lady raising her eyebrows and widening her eyes, look, the ministers and consuls of various countries rushed to mediate. Trenches have already been dug in Rehe, preparing to fight the enemy to the death, and the League of Nations' condition is improving day by day, much stronger than before.

In this world, you can only avoid being bullied if you are strong yourself. If you're like A Dou, just hoping that someone will right wrongs and draw a sword to help, humph, forget about it.

Two Good Mirrors 146

— Tu Hongxia

[Chinese Women, Please Look at Yourselves]

(1) Mrs. Matsuoka

Many days ago, the newspaper reported: [When Matsuoka left the country to go to Geneva, his old mother personally gave him a Japanese sword and instructed him to fight for the country, saying that if diplomacy failed at the League of Nations, he could commit suicide with the sword to show the spirit of the Yamato people.] Matsuoka took the sword and ran to Geneva. Seeing that Japanese diplomacy was in a stalemate, Matsuoka often sighed when he saw the sword given by his mother every time he returned to his residence. This sword is indeed valuable. It's both tragic and fervent, and especially we Chinese people who are afraid of death should emulate it.

In China, when a child is born, they are all regarded as their own source of wealth, a money tree. As long as this child grows up, is able to flatter, brag, and be corrupt, and knows how to make money, parents will definitely smile. No matter what society is like? What is the country like? This Mrs. Matsuoka takes her son's life and death very lightly and regards the country and the nation as important. In the vastness of China, I'm afraid you won't be able to find even half a person even if you wear out your iron shoes.

If the mothers of China give each of their children a sharp Chinese sword and instruct them: [If you don't kill your enemies, wash away the disgrace, and recover the] lost territory, then commit suicide with the sword and never come home again.]

If we can do that, China is guaranteed not to perish!

(2) Mrs. Noriko

Today, especially in the deformed society of China, it is really as rare as [phoenix feathers and unicorn horns] to find a woman who is truly virtuous and can help her husband succeed in his studies. Unexpectedly, in the three-island Japan! There is actually a Mrs. Noriko who stands out from the crowd.

Because her husband was working as a teaching assistant in economics at Kyoto Imperial University, burying himself in research all day long without producing anything, Mrs. Noriko secretly practiced driving a car and obtained a driver's license. She worked as a chauffeur during the day to make a living and took care of household chores at night so that her husband could concentrate on his studies. This is a commendable thing.

How dignified and happy is the wife of a university professor? How humble and painful is a chauffeur? However, in the eyes of this virtuous Mrs. Noriko, nothing is dignified, and nothing is happy. Only her husband's academic success is the most dignified and happiest thing. Alas! In the vast land of China, where can we find a second Mrs. Noriko?

Jade and Women 147

— Miaoshen

In our country's writing, jade has always been used to represent women. For example, [jade person] refers to a beautiful woman; for example, (jade appearance) refers to a woman's beauty. It can be seen that the meaning of the word jade is not only a metaphor for women, but also a metaphor for beautiful women. And women, not only regard themselves as jade, but also claim everything, such as [jade skin], [jade wrist], [jade thighs], [jade legs], everything on a woman's body is like jade. And they befriend jade, regard jade as the ultimate treasure, and wear jade on their bodies and on their heads. If jade had knowledge, it could be called infinite blessing! If jade didn't have the need of women, I'm afraid its value today would be little different from bricks and stones. So jade is not precious without women; women are not beautiful without jade! Therefore, a libertine in later generations defined it by saying: Jade is a woman, and a woman is jade.

From the dictionary, we can find that the ancient writing of the word [play] is [妧]. Someone asked: Why did the [妧] character change to the [play] character? There is also a meaning to this: because although women's rights in our country were not developed in the past, the heart of worshiping women was no less than that of modern people. Their reason was: How can a woman be played with by you? If you want to play, go play with jade! Therefore, the character [妧], which has a female radical, was changed to [play], which has a jade radical. It's a pity that the general public doesn't understand the original intention of this character-creating gentleman and still compares jade to women, endlessly entangled with what is beautiful jade and what is a beautiful woman. This is too ungrateful to the painstakingly transformed [play] character.

Novel

The Landlord 148

— Qin Shouou

"Good! Good, Brother Zhang!" Every blood vessel in the landlord's body was swelling, almost bursting. "Now, please take our Lao Liu and Lao Qi out to inform the residents of the village, and tell them to escape as soon as possible. If anyone is willing to stay here and fight to the death with the Japanese, please move into the manor and lie in ambush in the woods to guard it. Those who are unwilling should not be forced!"

The three people left like whirlwinds.

"Be careful! Be prepared!" The landlord, with his knife held horizontally, saw a group of spirited young people already lying in ambush in the woods, rubbing their fists and preparing to defend when his old partner carried him out of the manor. These were all [militia farmers] that he had trained over the years.

After the news that the landlord had ordered everyone to escape spread, the whole village knew that their lives were in danger. The situation was immediately chaotic. Men, women, old, young, who didn't want to escape? People flowed westward like a tide. Cries and shouts echoed the sounds of fighting in the distance. Chickens and dogs were also flying and running wildly in the streets. A total of fourteen people were willing to stay here, including one woman and one patient.

The patient was Brother Zhao. After sending his wife and children out of the village, he leaned on a crutch and slowly limped into the manor.

"Brother Zhao! What are you staying here for? Why don't you escape early?" Someone next to him asked.

"Although I can't go to battle, I can cook for you and do my best!" A hearty smile floated on Brother Zhao's golden face. "It turns out that the person who cooks can also go out to fight!"

"Brother Zhao is right!" Everyone was moved by him.

"Auntie! Why don't you leave?" Xiao Ling asked the woman very sincerely. The woman was the landlord's daughter, who was already a widow.

"What are you talking about! How could the landlord's daughter be willing to escape with others!" Auntie walked into the house as calmly as if she didn't know there were Japanese invaders coming, and her pace was as calm and slow as usual.

Brother Zhao and Auntie's encouragement gave everyone ten times more courage, and they held their weapons especially forcefully, quietly waiting for the time of bloody battle to come. The people in the village had all left, but there was still no news of the victory or defeat on the front line. "Xiao Ling! Do you hear how the shouts are getting closer?" The speaker was Xiao He, Xiao Ling's cousin.

Xiao Ling responded with silence. (5)

The Voice of National Salvation: My Personal View on Saving the Nation Through Aviation 149

— Tianxu Wosheng

Having read the *Shenbao* from February 15th of this year, the Aviation Association has organized two hundred fundraising teams, aiming to raise two million yuan in membership fees. The cost of purchasing aircraft, according to Mayor Wu's reply to the Chinese Women's Temperance Union, is approximately between one hundred thousand and one hundred fifty thousand per plane. According to Mr. Lin Wojiang, Japan currently has one thousand five hundred to one thousand six hundred aircraft, so we should have at least one thousand. Therefore, the cost of purchasing planes would require two hundred million yuan. The Association's fundraising only covers one percent of the required funds. However, I believe that everyone possesses a heart for national salvation. If four hundred million people each contribute half a yuan, even the poorest beggar, earning only one copper coin a day, could fulfill their responsibility in just a few months. As for those unable to contribute, such as infants in swaddling clothes, someone must bear the associated responsibility, so there is no need to worry about their inability to contribute. For example, the head of an eight-person household should contribute four yuan, fulfilling their due obligation. Those with greater means can contribute several times that amount, based on their conscience and willingness, without facing difficulties. As for the payment method, it would be best if the government immediately printed a batch of aviation savings certificates, imitating postage stamps, divided into denominations of half a yuan, five yuan, and fifty yuan. These should be distributed to post offices across the country and sold like postage stamps. People could deposit aviation national salvation savings at any post office or mailbox, receiving a certificate equivalent to the amount deposited for verification purposes. Simultaneously, postmen could serve as volunteer fundraisers, carrying these certificates while delivering mail to conveniently solicit donations. They would submit their collections to the post office daily, ensuring success and quick results along their routes. Those who have fulfilled this obligation can affix the certificate to their door or in a visible place, demonstrating their patriotism and fostering a sense of glory. Since the anniversary of the January 28th Incident, the public is generally aware of the necessity of saving the nation through aviation. However, there are several concerns among the public: Some believe that such national salvation donations have been launched many times, but few have yielded satisfactory results, leading to a cold attitude. Others wonder where these donations will ultimately go and whether they will materialize into tangible results, causing them to hesitate. Some are ashamed of their limited ability to contribute significantly, thinking their small contributions are insignificant. Still others believe that there are too many fundraisers who frequently visit their homes, with no clear standards, leading to misunderstandings and suspicions. In my humble opinion, all of these concerns can be addressed. If the public knows the required contribution is only half a yuan per person, and those who can afford to contribute for ten, a hundred, a thousand, or ten thousand people are likely to do so, and those who have not fulfilled their share will feel ashamed and strive to meet their obligations. Even if parents have already fulfilled their children's share, the children may voluntarily save money from candy and toys to purchase national salvation certificates, demonstrating their ability to contribute. I expect the post offices to be as crowded as the roads of Shanyin, collecting and remitting funds every ten days, reaching a considerable sum. If it is announced to the public within a month that a hundred aircraft have been purchased, it will inspire many to enthusiastically contribute, and those with extra resources will volunteer to donate again, without needing further solicitation. If someone affixes this certificate to a black armband to commemorate the September 18th Incident, I believe it will create a stronger impression than giving speeches, as all acts of awakening operate in this way. As for aviation mail, it can also be utilized accordingly. Defensive measures are like training soldiers for a thousand days to use them at a critical moment. In ancient times, soldiers were integrated with farmers; why can't we integrate anti-aircraft fighters into the postal service today? I sincerely hope that our government will consider my humble suggestions and implement them resolutely!

A Bird's-Eye View of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals in Shanghai in the Last Decade (Continued)

Pang Jingzhou

In addition to the aforementioned public and private hospitals, there are also clinics that call themselves hospitals but cannot accommodate patients, easily causing misunderstandings in society and providing opportunities for unscrupulous doctors to deceive people for profit. I would like to take this opportunity to clarify: The term "hospital" is not originally a Chinese term. The name "Tai Hospital" (a collection of imperial physicians) was used during the monarchical era. Since it was used to translate the Western word "Hospital," the narrow interpretation in people's minds seems to be a place that accommodates patients for treatment and recovery. However, government officials have not explicitly stipulated the qualifications for a hospital or stated that the name cannot be misused. As the saying goes, "If the name is not correct, the words will not ring true," and thus disputes arise.

Many doctors hang a "hospital" sign outside their personal clinics, either calling it "So-and-So Hospital" or choosing names like "Ankang Boji," but in reality, they cannot accommodate a single inpatient. In particular, general practitioners take advantage of the notion that "hospitals have greater prestige than individual practitioners" and collectively hang up hospital signs. As a result, the glass windows on Fourth Avenue are filled with the words "hospital," and the advertisement columns in newspapers are filled with hospital names. The most ridiculous thing is to borrow the name of a well-known hospital elsewhere as a way to attract customers. For example, there is a Peking Union Medical College Hospital in Beijing that covers hundreds of acres, and there is also a "Peking Union Medical College Hospital" in Shanghai that occupies two rooms. There is a Guangji Hospital in Hangzhou that is built on mountains and rivers, and there is also a "Guangji Hospital" on a corner in Shanghai. There is a Gospel Hospital in Suzhou with beautiful scenery, and there is also a "Gospel Hospital" in Shanghai with brilliant electric lights. Not only is it written clearly in Chinese characters, but also a Western-language banner is added, and the prices for each department are marked on the wall so that potential patients can understand at a glance, truly making a fool of ourselves in front of foreigners and creating a spectacle in society. However, there is also a basis for some of our new medical practitioners to call clinics hospitals. According to Japanese custom, a place where a doctor practices individually is called a "hospital," and a place that accommodates inpatients is called a "sanatorium." Therefore, hospitals such as "Shimizu" and "Shinozaki" in the Hongkou area do not necessarily accept inpatients, and the fact that Fumin Hospital does not call itself a sanatorium has already accommodated Chinese customs. In this anti-Japanese trend, I want to advise my colleagues not to use Japanese customs as a basis for calling clinics hospitals, so as not to disrupt our already "agreed-upon name."

However, people in society have changed their previous understanding of hospitals because of this confusion in the medical community. I am often asked during social gatherings, and I have heard other doctors being asked the same question: "I have heard a lot about you! Where is your big doctor's hospital?" It seems that a doctor must have a hospital, and only those with a hospital are big doctors. Therefore, I advocate that in the near future, the Health Bureau, the Medical Association, and other organizations should work together with the concession authorities to investigate the public and private hospitals in Shanghai, indicating the chief physician, the departments of diagnosis and treatment, the number of beds, the level of service, and the fees charged. A large-scale disclosure in the newspapers can analyze the public's perception and facilitate patients in choosing the appropriate medical care, which is not a small matter.

Scientific Ways to Preserve Life (7) Yu Songyun 150

(10) Method for Estimating the Date of Childbirth

Calculate from the first day of the last menstrual period to 280 days, which is the estimated date of childbirth. The calculation method is to add seven days to the first day of the last menstrual period and add nine months to the month number, or subtract three months from it, which is the estimated date of childbirth:

(1) Assuming the first day of the last menstrual period is September 21st:

Day Day Day

21 + 7 = 28, i.e., June 28th

Month Month Month

9 - 3 = 6, which is the estimated date of childbirth

(2) Assuming the first day of the last menstrual period is January 5th:

Day Day Day

5 + 7 = 12, i.e., October 12th

Month Month Month

1 + 9 = 10, which is the estimated date of childbirth

This calculation method is simple and clear, and everyone can easily calculate it.

There is also a prediction table, which is quite simple. The table is as follows:

This table is based on the date of the last menstrual period. Add the corresponding number in the table to get the result.

For example, if the last menstrual period was January 20th, then the predicted delivery date is October 27th. If the last menstrual period was December 1st, then the predicted delivery date is September 7th of the following year, and so on.

(11) Childbirth (Labor)

Childbirth is the expulsion of the fetus and its appendages from the pregnant woman, commonly known as labor. Generally, 280 days is considered the normal period of childbirth. During this period, there is a force of expulsion that allows the fetus to be delivered naturally and causes the uterus to contract, also known as the force of delivery, which is labor pain, abdominal pressure, vaginal wall, pelvic floor, round ligaments, and fallopian tube muscles, all of which contract.

(A) Labor Pain

Labor pain is the periodic contraction of the uterus during childbirth, causing pain, hence the name labor pain.

Labor pain is the beginning of childbirth and promotes the process of childbirth. It can cause the separation and expulsion of the ovum, facilitating childbirth.

Premonitory labor pain is the slight uterine contraction that often occurs near the end of pregnancy, called premonitory labor pain. Primiparas (women giving birth for the first time) often experience a sense of tension or slight pain during premonitory labor pain, but multiparas (women giving birth for the second time or more) often have no pain. In premonitory labor pain, it occurs only once or twice at first, and as the time of delivery approaches, the number of labor pains increases, but the onset and interval are generally not very uniform, and the contraction force is very weak. If the labor pain intensifies, it is often mistaken for the beginning of childbirth, and one must carefully distinguish between them.

(B) The First Stage of Labor… Opening Stage

The first stage of labor begins with labor pain, called the opening stage of labor pain, which starts with repeated uniformity and continues until the cervix is fully opened. At this time, the uterus gradually contracts, the labor pain gradually intensifies, the duration of the labor pain is 30 to 50 seconds, or perhaps longer, the interval is 10 to 15 minutes, or perhaps 2 to 5 minutes. As the labor pain intensifies, the cervix gradually dilates, and the membrane also separates from the uterus. There is often bleeding on the separation surface, so when it is discharged, there is often mucus mixed with blood, which is a sign that the cervix is dilated.

(1) How can the cervix dilate? The aforementioned separated membrane bulges like a cyst and enters the cervix, thus the cervix slowly dilates. This is the amniotic sac, which stores amniotic fluid (sac water). The amniotic sac is tense during labor pain and relaxed during intervals. Every time there is labor pain, the size and tension of the amniotic sac will increase, and it will press open the cervix from above. After the cervix is dilated, the edge shrinks upward. At this time, the baby's head of a primipara embeds into the pelvis, and the baby's head of a multipara is still moving at the pelvic inlet, but during labor pain, they are all fixed at the pelvic inlet.

(2) There is a sound when the amniotic sac ruptures. During this period, labor pains repeatedly intensify, and the pregnant woman suddenly becomes terrified, loses appetite, or even does not eat, feels cold and afraid of cold, and often has nausea and vomiting. The more the cervix dilates, the more intense the labor pain becomes, and the amniotic sac is abnormally tense. The amniotic sac no longer relaxes during the intervals of labor pain. All tensions reach the extreme. At this moment, the membrane suddenly ruptures, and at the same time, the fore sac water (amniotic fluid) is ejected. This is the rupture of the sac. The sac water weighs about 30 cm when the sac ruptures, and there is a sound.

(3) False amniotic fluid… False amniotic fluid, commonly known as "follicle birth," is the outflow of liquid accumulated between the decidua and chorion, which is mistaken for fore amniotic fluid, or ruptures above, so the sac water leaks, but the membrane has not ruptured.

(4) The timing of the rupture of the sac… If it has already ruptured during premonitory labor pain, it is called early rupture of membranes. If the cervix has not yet dilated to 5 cm and the presenting part of the fetus has not yet reached the pelvic inlet, but the sac water has already ruptured, this is early rupture of membranes. (5) The danger of early rupture of membranes… The dilation of the uterus after rupture of membranes relies entirely on the presenting part of the fetus to promote it, so it is very slow, and the amniotic fluid leaks continuously. If there is an early rupture of membranes, then the fetus is closely attached to the uterine wall, which may lead to a dangerous situation.

(6) Delayed rupture of membranes… The cervix has fully dilated, but the amniotic sac does not rupture. This is because the labor pain has gradually decreased, causing it to bulge outside the vulva. The placenta is pulled by it, so a part of it is separated and bleeds, hindering the fetal blood circulation, or the fetus is completely wrapped in the membrane and delivered. If the membrane is not cut open, then the fetus will inevitably suffocate and die.

(7) After the rupture of the sac… The labor pain often rests for a moment, and then occurs strongly again. At that time, the baby's head penetrates further into the pelvic cavity and moves forward to the second stage of labor.

Talking About Phlegm, Part Three

Yu Yunxiu

The theories about the symptoms of phlegm disease have become extremely chaotic and bizarre since the Jin and Yuan dynasties. I will not cite them all, but record the most notable ones to show the general idea.

Chen Wuzhe's *Three Causes Formula* states: ["Coughing, asthma, vomiting, diarrhea, dizziness, restlessness, palpitations, worries, hot and cold sensations, pain, swelling, fullness, abdominal masses, urinary retention, obstruction, like wind, like epilepsy, none are not caused by phlegm and fluid."]

Wang Yinjun said: ["Or headache, dizziness, eye movement, ear ringing, or twitching of the mouth and eyes, itching or pain in the eyebrows and ears, or wind-like swelling and hardening of the limbs, with pain that seems not to be pain, or itching and pain in the teeth and cheeks, teeth floating and pain varying, or belching, acid reflux, heart burning, or pain or hiccups, or difficulty in swallowing, unable to cough up or swallow down, the phlegm is like ink, like broken cotton, peach gum, or clam meat, or the heart feels like frozen iron, cold pain in the heart, or strange dreams, or weakness in the feet and wrists, sudden pain in the lower back and joints, or pain in the limbs and bones that is difficult to name, with no specific location, or numbness in the hands and pain in the arms, like rheumatism, or a cold sensation like a thread rising on the back,

Page 14

or the whole body feels like lying on thorns, or sticky, itchy eyes, canker sores, sore throat, etc., or cervical lymph node enlargement, like scrofula, or two energies intertwining between the chest and abdomen, stuffiness, like smoke rising, hot flashes in the head and face, or loss of will, madness, or stroke paralysis, or chronic debilitating diseases, or toxic leg qi, or palpitations in the heart, like being chased by a tall man, or coughing and vomiting, or vomiting cold saliva, green water, or black juice, even lung abscesses, intestinal toxins, constipation, lameness, generally internal and external diseases, all kinds are caused by phlegm, the symptoms are different and difficult to describe in detail. Since body fluids congeal into phlegm, they no longer moisten the triple energizer, so the mouth is dry, the throat is dry, the stool is constipated, the face is like withered bones, the hair is scorched, and women have amenorrhea because of this."] This is the most complex theory of phlegm disease symptoms (Xu Chunfu's *Comprehensive Medicine of Ancient and Modern Times* and Sun Dongsu's *Red Water Primal Ball* cite Wang Yinjun, the theory is even more complicated, here quoted from Liu Zonghou's *Jade Pivot Subtle Meaning* and Shen Langzhong's *Collection of Disease Mechanisms*).

The *Golden Chamber* already mentions symptoms of phlegm and fluid that overflow beyond stomach and intestinal diseases, such as numbness in the hands and feet, arthralgia in the limbs, and the like. And the face is flushed and hot as if drunk, and the like. These are all concurrent symptoms, but all attributed to phlegm and fluid, which is already untrustworthy. As for Wang Yinjun, he attributes all internal and surgical diseases, neurological diseases, and mental illnesses to phlegm, in order to expand the efficacy of his *Tumbling Phlegm Pills*, which is extremely absurd. Liu Zonghou then cites the words of *Pulse Classic* and *Living People's Book* to clarify that Yinjun's statements are not slander, and those who talk about phlegm later seem to be in a net and unable to escape.

As for the causes of phlegm, Zhang Zihe divides it into wind phlegm, heat phlegm, damp phlegm, alcohol phlegm, and food phlegm in five categories. Chen Wuzhe uses the seven emotions as internal causes, the six evils as external causes, and diet, sex, and exercise as neither internal nor external causes. Danxi distinguishes between heat, qi, fright, continuous drinking and overeating, summer heat, injury from cold things, spleen deficiency, and addiction to alcohol. There are also terms such as wet phlegm, old phlegm, depressed phlegm, and stubborn phlegm. According to the theory of phlegm disease symptoms, there is no disease that is not caused by phlegm. According to the theory of the causes of phlegm disease, there is no cause that cannot produce phlegm. Later, Liu Songfeng spoke of epidemic diseases, and then there was no disease that was not epidemic. Guo Youtao spoke of sha diseases, and then there was no disease that was not sha. All of them follow the old wisdom of the Jin and Yuan dynasties' theory of phlegm.

As for the causes of phlegm formation, the people of the Han and Tang dynasties only said that it was caused by the accumulation of water and fluids. The people of the Song dynasty believed that it was caused by the coagulation and turbidity of body fluids. This theory probably originated from Pang Anchang. It was also believed that it was caused by the accumulation of saliva to form fluid. This theory can be seen in Chen Wuzhe. Since then, when talking about phlegm, it is completely regarded as viscous saliva and thick, turbid sputum, and no longer regarded as water and fluid as phlegm. What is even more strange is that what is sticky and thick is regarded as phlegm, and what is clear and thin is regarded as fluid. This is what later generations commonly say, but Chen Wuzhe has the saying ["Saliva congeals to form fluid"]. If fluid is formed by the coagulation of saliva, then fluid is thicker than saliva, which is no different from phlegm. That is, even the water and fluid of the ancients are also regarded as viscous phlegm.

In short, the phlegm and fluid in the *Golden Chamber* only refers to the water in the stomach and intestines. Later generations recognized sticky saliva and thick, turbid sputum as phlegm, so the symptoms they saw were naturally different from those in the *Golden Chamber*. However, they did not dare to delete or modify the symptoms of water and fluid mentioned in the *Golden Chamber*. Therefore, they were compatible and inclusive, combined with the saliva in the lungs, and the theory of phlegm and fluid began to be confused. At the time of the flourishing of Jin and Yuan dynasties' fantasy and metaphysical theories, the arguments were boundless. Then, the mucus secreted by mucous membrane inflammation was also included, such as dysentery. Then, the acute neurological disorders, where the secretion of the trachea increased accordingly, were also included, such as stroke, infantile convulsion, epilepsy, and morning vomiting of alcoholics. Extending it further, diseases that had absolutely no relationship with water and mucus were also brought in, such as the inability to move the arm, numbness in the hand, and neurological symptoms such as wind noise behind the head, cicada chirping in the ears, and palpitations in the heart as if afraid of being caught. Therefore, the theory of phlegm disease is chaotic, bizarre, and impossible to investigate.

Utilizing Chinese Medicine in the Western Manner (Continued) by Zhou Mengbai 151

(VII) Star Anise (Large Anise) Anisum Stellatum

This product originally comes from plants of the Magnolia family (Magnoliaceae), specifically the mature fruit of the star anise (Illicum verum Hooker filius), produced in various southwestern provinces of our country.

Shape: This product is a fruit composed of six to eleven follicles, though most commonly it has eight, hence the name "star anise." Each follicle is shaped like a small, opened boat, with its base attached to a common central axis. Below the central axis is a hook-shaped fruit stalk. The outside appears reddish-brown and has numerous wrinkles, while the inside is smooth, lighter in color, and glossy. The distal end forms a blunt bird's beak shape, containing a single, oval-shaped seed. It has a pleasant aroma and a sweet taste.

Composition: When this product is distilled with water, it yields volatile star anise oil, approximately five percent. This oil is composed of anethole, safrole, and anisic acid, among other substances. It also contains sugar, mucilage, and fatty oil.

Uses: This product is a stimulant or carminative, commonly used as a flavoring or deodorizing agent.

(Appendix: Old Theories) It is acrid and hot, entering the kidney and bladder meridians, soothing the Dantian, replenishing deficiencies in the Life Gate, stimulating the appetite, stopping vomiting, treating cold Qi in the small intestine, scrotal hernia, and scrotal pain. There is mention of Japanese star anise, which is the fruit of _Illicium Religiosum Sieb et Zuco_, also known as the shikimi fruit. Its shape is not very different from star anise, but it is slightly smaller, and the tip of the boat-shaped follicle is sharper and curved. Its aroma is completely different from star anise, resembling cardamom or cubeb pepper. It contains shikimic acid and is highly toxic. It must not be mixed into star anise. Previously, at Jiangsu Medical University, there was a case in Suzhou where someone died from consuming star anise. Upon examination, it was found to be not star anise but the poisonous Japanese star anise, i.e., shikimi fruit. Some pharmacies use it as a counterfeit drug due to its similar shape and lower price. Therefore, one should be especially careful when using star anise.

Diseases: Common Knowledge Q&A

(Continued) by Cheng Hanzhang

(III) Measles (Commonly Known as Shazi or Yuzi)

Question: What is measles? What is it called in Western languages? Answer: Measles is commonly known as Yuzi or Shazi. The English name is Measles, the German name is Masern, and the Latin name is Morbilli.

Question: What is the pathogen of measles?

Answer: It has not yet been discovered, but it is likely an ultramicroscopic microbe.

Question: Where does this pathogen exist? Answer: It exists in the blood, tears, phlegm, nasal discharge, saliva, and skin scales of patients.

Question: Which type of person is most susceptible to measles? Answer: Children are most susceptible.

Question: How is it transmitted?

Answer: It is transmitted through cohabitation with patients, close proximity, or inhalation of airborne pathogens.

Question: Why are children most susceptible to measles?

Answer: Because humans are all susceptible to measles; once measles is contracted, lifelong immunity is usually acquired. Therefore, almost all children get infected, while most adults have already had the disease and are no longer susceptible.

Question: During which season is this disease most prevalent? Answer: It tends to be more prevalent in the spring.

Question: How many days after measles viruses are contracted does illness develop?

Answer: It takes about ten days of incubation before the illness develops. Question: During the period of illness, into how many phases can we divide it? Answer: It can be divided into three phases: the prodromal phase, the eruptive phase, and the recovery phase.

Question: What are the symptoms of the prodromal phase?

Answer: The patient's face is slightly swollen, and symptoms of inflammation appear in the conjunctiva, nasal cavity, pharynx, larynx, and bronchi. There is photophobia, tearing, sneezing, epistaxis, hoarseness, coughing, etc. This situation lasts for about three or four days, then mucous membrane spots and Koplik's spots appear. This is a symptom unique to measles.

Question: What are Koplik's spots?

Answer: Koplik's spots are white spots that appear on the oral mucosa opposite the molars, the size of pinheads, surrounded by a red halo.

Question: What is the body temperature like during this period?

Answer: The body temperature rises with shivering or chills in the first few days, then drops briefly, and then rises again from the third day, like a staircase.

Question: What are the symptoms of the eruptive phase?

Answer: When the body develops a rash, the body temperature rises further, showing persistent fever or remittent fever patterns; when the rash has fully emerged, the fever dissipates.

Question: What does the rash on the body look like? Answer: The skin rash first appears on the face, head, auricles, etc., followed by the neck, trunk, and limbs. Initially, the rash consists of blood-filled spots the size of pinheads, consistent with hair follicles; later, they gradually enlarge and merge, rising slightly above the skin surface, becoming papules that are light pink to dark red. The rash is most pronounced on the third day of the eruptive phase. The mucous membrane spots, on the other hand, subside when the skin rash becomes noticeable. Koplik's spots are also unclear. Question: What is the recovery phase like?

Answer: During the recovery phase, the body temperature is normal, and the skin rash gradually fades in the order it appeared, with desquamation, and then various symptoms disappear. Question: Are there any other complications during the recovery phase?

Answer: Yes, there are. Most develop bronchitis, or even pneumonia, which can be very severe. (To be continued)
